<br />
<div id="page-2426">
<h3><a name="page-2426">Saturday, June  9, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day and clear and <span class='line-break'> </span> dry. Oh how we need rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> The men planted some<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco. I [sic] it can't live if<span class='line-break'> </span> it don't rain soon.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ray Booker played with <span class='line-break'> </span> Franklin all evening. They<span class='line-break'> </span> went in the garden and<span class='line-break'> </span> pulled them an onion and <span class='line-break'> </span> wanted to eat them. I <span class='line-break'> </span> did not let Franklin. <span class='line-break'> </span> Thought it might make him<span class='line-break'> </span> sick. Mabel has not bin<span class='line-break'> </span> so well today. Hope she<span class='line-break'> </span> won't get sick. <span class='line-break'> </span> I have bin very busy<span class='line-break'> </span> today. Tried to sweep the<span class='line-break'> </span> floor most all over<span class='line-break'> </span> the house.<span class='line-break'> </span> That is a job for me.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lawson Emerson is coming<span class='line-break'> </span> up here tonight to<span class='line-break'> </span> go fishing.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2428">
<h3><a name="page-2428">Sunday, June 10, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Johnsons.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and the children went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Cedar Forest. They stoppe<span class='line-break'> </span> at the church. Then went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Jim Powers for<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. Jim staid <span class='line-break'> </span> at home. Mrs. Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> and Mrs Anderson come to<span class='line-break'> </span> see me. I would of bin <span class='line-break'> </span> glad to seen them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Gordon and Earl come<span class='line-break'> </span> after me and carried<span class='line-break'> </span> me to George Blains. <span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie was there and Earl<span class='line-break'> </span> and his wife was there.<span class='line-break'> </span> Dorathy and Ruth <span class='line-break'> </span> Worshan was there. They <span class='line-break'> </span> are pretty girls. <span class='line-break'> </span> I was so glad to <span class='line-break'> </span> get to go. Jim and I was <span class='line-break'> </span> eating dinner when <span class='line-break'> </span> they come. Cary and<span class='line-break'> </span> Shirly was with them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Frances was there. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2429">
<h3><a name="page-2429">Monday, June 11, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good rain today.<span class='line-break'> </span> The men replanted<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco. I am so glad<span class='line-break'> </span> that it has rained. We<span class='line-break'> </span> could not make any<span class='line-break'> </span> thing to eat if it had<span class='line-break'> </span> not rained soon.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have bin busy doing<span class='line-break'> </span> most nothing. The children<span class='line-break'> </span> has had to stay in<span class='line-break'> </span> all the morning. They<span class='line-break'> </span> tried to see what they<span class='line-break'> </span> could do.<span class='line-break'> </span> I sewed a little this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I wrote Mrs Lou<span class='line-break'> </span> [Terry?] today.<span class='line-break'> </span> This has bin one of the worst<span class='line-break'> </span> seasons that I have ever known.<span class='line-break'> </span> There is not plants to plant<span class='line-break'> </span> the crop.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2431">
<h3><a name="page-2431">Tuesday, June 12, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day and some <span class='line-break'> </span> rain. We have rain enough<span class='line-break'> </span> for now. They finished planted<span class='line-break'> </span> all the land they had fixed<span class='line-break'> </span> up and give some plants away.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad that they had them.<span class='line-break'> </span> We had fried chicken<span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner. The children <span class='line-break'> </span> caught them for me.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr. Mayhew and two of<span class='line-break'> </span> his little boy helped plant <span class='line-break'> </span> some. <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Les Booker come to<span class='line-break'> </span> Normans for plants.<span class='line-break'> </span> Plants is so hard<span class='line-break'> </span> to get this year.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am writing early<span class='line-break'> </span> to night. I got supper<span class='line-break'> </span> early as it was raining<span class='line-break'> </span> so that they could<span class='line-break'> </span> not work. Edna got<span class='line-break'> </span> a letter from Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Bessie Hobson to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> She said that Mary <span class='line-break'> </span> would graduate soon.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2430">
<h3><a name="page-2430">Wednesday, June 13, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Cloudy all day and some<span class='line-break'> </span> rain. This morning Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> and Jim replanted some <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco. This evening Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> staid with the children.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Oscar<span class='line-break'> </span> Brumfield kindly<span class='line-break'> </span> carried Mr Kellie <span class='line-break'> </span> and Mrs Kellie with him<span class='line-break'> </span> fishing. I went with<span class='line-break'> </span> them. I was glad to go.<span class='line-break'> </span> We did not catch any<span class='line-break'> </span> fish the river. We could <span class='line-break'> </span> not fish there so we<span class='line-break'> </span> come back to the creek. <span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Kellie fell and broke<span class='line-break'> </span> her arm and we come<span class='line-break'> </span> home as quick as we <span class='line-break'> </span> well could. I am so<span class='line-break'> </span> sorry that whe was hurt. <span class='line-break'> </span> I would do something<span class='line-break'> </span> to help her if there<span class='line-break'> </span> was any thing that I<span class='line-break'> </span> could do. I was so glad<span class='line-break'> </span> to go. Mr Kellie was there.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2433">
<h3><a name="page-2433">Thursday, June 14, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Jim and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> plowed all the morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben cut wheat for Mr<span class='line-break'> </span> Booker. The children was<span class='line-break'> </span> invited to Mr. Rufus Carrs<span class='line-break'> </span> to a birth day party and <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben could not carry them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna cried. I wish they<span class='line-break'> </span> could of went. <span class='line-break'> </span> We had a vegetable<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. Snaps, potatoes,<span class='line-break'> </span> peas, beets. I had an onion.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children was at<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Bookers all the<span class='line-break'> </span> evening. This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> has seemed long <span class='line-break'> </span> to me here by my<span class='line-break'> </span> self. John Ward <span class='line-break'> </span> and Henry thined corn<span class='line-break'> </span> all day.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-2432">
<h3><a name="page-2432">Friday, June 15, 1923 (original)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Then<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried them to Marvin<span class='line-break'> </span> Smiths. Jim would not go.<span class='line-break'> </span> I think they enjoyed<span class='line-break'> </span> their visit. I know I did.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr. Emmet Smith nearly<span class='line-break'> </span> all of the family come<span class='line-break'> </span> to Marvins. Carrie had<span class='line-break'> </span> cake and pickle enough <span class='line-break'> </span> for all of us. It was<span class='line-break'> </span> very nice.<span class='line-break'> </span> When we got home<span class='line-break'> </span> Lee and Jim was on the<span class='line-break'> </span> porch talking. I got<span class='line-break'> </span> supper as quick as I <span class='line-break'> </span> could but Lee would <span class='line-break'> </span> not stay. I went to<span class='line-break'> </span> sleep and dropped my <span class='line-break'> </span> pen and made a<span class='line-break'> </span> blot on my<span class='line-break'> </span> book.</p>

<h3><a name="page-2443">Thursday, June 21, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very hot day. We had<span class='line-break'> </span> a thunder cloud but<span class='line-break'> </span> no rain to do any good. <span class='line-break'> </span> I hope it may rain soon. <span class='line-break'> </span> We need it so bad.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben mowed some oat<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning and cut some<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. He let all<span class='line-break'> </span> the children go. Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> and John and Henry worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on the tobacco. Jim [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> the potatoes. It needed<span class='line-break'> </span> nearly 100 slips to <span class='line-break'> </span> replant the slips. <span class='line-break'> </span> I made Franklin a <span class='line-break'> </span> middie to day. I don't<span class='line-break'> </span> know hoe it will <span class='line-break'> </span> look but hope it will<span class='line-break'> </span> do very well. <div id="page-2447">
<h3><a name="page-2447">Monday, June 25, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. No rain <span class='line-break'> </span> yet. Jim and Ben hauled<span class='line-break'> </span> up the wheat and stacked<span class='line-break'> </span> and Jim got up some <span class='line-break'> </span> oats. Late this evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to Cedar<span class='line-break'> </span> Forest. He carried the <span class='line-break'> </span> three least children <span class='line-break'> </span> and I. We bought<span class='line-break'> </span> two bushels of meal<span class='line-break'> </span> from George Hutchenson.<span class='line-break'> </span> Paid #2:20 cts for<span class='line-break'> </span> it. We carried 6 dozen<span class='line-break'> </span> eggs to Thomsons. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to Jim Powers<span class='line-break'> </span> and staid a little while.<span class='line-break'> </span> Tonight when I got ready<span class='line-break'> </span> to write gathered up my<span class='line-break'> </span> things to write I turned <span class='line-break'> </span> the ink over in my<span class='line-break'> </span> lap and spill a [pon? or upon] <span class='line-break'> </span> of it. Edna got me <span class='line-break'> </span> a pan of water. I washed<span class='line-break'> </span> all of it out that I could.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2448">
<h3><a name="page-2448">Tuesday, June 26, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very windy day and<span class='line-break'> </span> hard on the growing<span class='line-break'> </span> things. Jim and Ben finished<span class='line-break'> </span> getting up the oats. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben mowed some.<span class='line-break'> </span> Two men come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> the boys today. Candidates.<span class='line-break'> </span> The county is full of <span class='line-break'> </span> men wanting office.<span class='line-break'> </span> No one come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> us today. I get so lone<span class='line-break'> </span> some for some one to<span class='line-break'> </span> talk to. I sent Edna <span class='line-break'> </span> to Mrs. Bookers with<span class='line-break'> </span> some meal an dcoffee <span class='line-break'> </span> that I had roasted.<span class='line-break'> </span> [Carrol?] was sick.<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope he may get <span class='line-break'> </span> well soon. I sent the<span class='line-break'> </span> clothes to Lelia by<span class='line-break'> </span> John.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2449">
<h3><a name="page-2449">Wednesday, June 27, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear hot day<span class='line-break'> </span> most of the day. A little <span class='line-break'> </span> cloudy right at night. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben mowed some and <span class='line-break'> </span> got up some hay. All <span class='line-break'> </span> three of them plowed<span class='line-break'> </span> some this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I cooked snaps. Can't<span class='line-break'> </span> get many more until it<span class='line-break'> </span> rains. oh that we could <span class='line-break'> </span> have a good rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children made them<span class='line-break'> </span> a pond in the branch<span class='line-break'> </span> to play in. They have <span class='line-break'> </span> a good time playing.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got up the onions<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. The children<span class='line-break'> </span> helped get them to the <span class='line-break'> </span> house. They are fine.<span class='line-break'> </span> The onions was planted<span class='line-break'> </span> the 27th of October and <span class='line-break'> </span> got up the 27 of June.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children want to <span class='line-break'> </span> sleep on a pallet to<span class='line-break'> </span> night.</p>

</div>

<div id="page-2451">
<h3><a name="page-2451">Thursday, June 28, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. The wind<span class='line-break'> </span> has blowed most all day. <span class='line-break'> </span> The boys mowed some<span class='line-break'> </span> and hauled up some hay. <span class='line-break'> </span> The Wooding land was <span class='line-break'> </span> solde today. Jim and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> did not go to the sale.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr. [?] Carter bought<span class='line-break'> </span> home place.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children has had<span class='line-break'> </span> a good time playing. <span class='line-break'> </span> I made Mabel a <span class='line-break'> </span> little suit to play<span class='line-break'> </span> in the water with. <span class='line-break'> </span> I think it look good<span class='line-break'> </span> on her. Lelia Ward<span class='line-break'> </span> sent the clothes home<span class='line-break'> </span> by John. They are o.k. <span class='line-break'> </span> Sam [C?llans] was <span class='line-break'> </span> here today trying to<span class='line-break'> </span> find plants. Every thing <span class='line-break'> </span> is drying up.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-2450">
<h3><a name="page-2450">Friday, June 29, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Cloudy <span class='line-break'> </span> most of the day. No Rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben finish mowing today<span class='line-break'> </span> and they hauled and <span class='line-break'> </span> put the hay in the <span class='line-break'> </span> house. This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried me and<span class='line-break'> </span> three children to Gretna.<span class='line-break'> </span> I bought several <span class='line-break'> </span> things. I would of liked<span class='line-break'> </span> to go to see Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> but did not have time.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie Reynols come<span class='line-break'> </span> while I was gone. I am<span class='line-break'> </span> sorry not to have seen<span class='line-break'> </span> her. Will go and see<span class='line-break'> </span> her soon if nothing happens.<span class='line-break'> </span> We met[?Alma] and Lizzie<span class='line-break'> </span> comeing this way. Don't <span class='line-break'> </span> know where they went.<span class='line-break'> </span> I phoned to hear from<span class='line-break'> </span> Lottie Craddock. She<span class='line-break'> </span> think she will have<span class='line-break'> </span> company Sunday.</p>

<div id="page-2452">
<h3><a name="page-2452">Saturday, June 30, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. No rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> You never see the crop<span class='line-break'> </span> need rain worse.<span class='line-break'> </span> I cooked dried beans<span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner and I am <span class='line-break'> </span> glad to have themn to cook.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have plenty of chickens<span class='line-break'> </span> [lang?] enough to kill.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Henry and John Ward<span class='line-break'> </span> plowed over some corn.<span class='line-break'> </span> They worked tobacco<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Christenia Reynols<span class='line-break'> </span> and Doris Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> come a while this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening. They looked<span class='line-break'> </span> [frest?] and good. <div id="page-2453">
<h3><a name="page-2453">Sunday, July  1, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy morning. Did not<span class='line-break'> </span> rain long. I hope it may<span class='line-break'> </span> rain a gain tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and family come<span class='line-break'> </span> today. I was very glad<span class='line-break'> </span> I had cooked our dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> when they got here.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie brought two chickens<span class='line-break'> </span> ready to fry and a cake<span class='line-break'> </span> so we had dinner aplenty <span class='line-break'> </span> with very little trouble.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to Sunday<span class='line-break'> </span> school. Lawson Emerson<span class='line-break'> </span> come home with him.<span class='line-break'> </span> They eat dinner and <span class='line-break'> </span> them and Jo Edmons<span class='line-break'> </span> and Reese went to<span class='line-break'> </span> get in the water <span class='line-break'> </span> some where.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel went to sleep<span class='line-break'> </span> be fore sundow and I<span class='line-break'> </span> guess she will sleep<span class='line-break'> </span> until morning.</p>

<div class="page-content">

Then <span class='line-break'> </span> chopped in the tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> The threshing machine<span class='line-break'> </span> is in the neighborhood.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry and John Ward<span class='line-break'> </span> went to help. They<span class='line-break'> </span> eat dinner at Jessie<span class='line-break'> </span> Hutchersons.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate Harvey come to<span class='line-break'> </span> see us today. <div id="page-2455">
<h3><a name="page-2455">Tuesday, July  3, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> and Ben plowed tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and the children went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Strait Stone this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening. I picked a few<span class='line-break'> </span> black berries this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Want to preserve them<span class='line-break'> </span> in the morning if I can.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lelia Ward come here this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening for a hen. Said<span class='line-break'> </span> she had to fix a basket<span class='line-break'> </span> for a pick nick tomorrow. <span class='line-break'> </span> I sent 7 doz eggs<span class='line-break'> </span> to the store to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> They paid 25 cts per <span class='line-break'> </span> doz. Edna bought two<span class='line-break'> </span> bowls to day. I am<span class='line-break'> </span> pleased with them. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben hates to take us<span class='line-break'> </span> any where so bad <span class='line-break'> </span> that he spoils all the pleasure.</p>

<div id="page-2456">
<h3><a name="page-2456">Wednesday, July  4, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. No rain<span class='line-break'> </span> yet. Ben and Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Gretna. They had a big<span class='line-break'> </span> tim. They eat dinner with<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and Carrie. Jim did<span class='line-break'> </span> not go. He worked most of <span class='line-break'> </span> the day. I made three<span class='line-break'> </span> quarts of black berrie<span class='line-break'> </span> preserves and killed two<span class='line-break'> </span> and fried them and<span class='line-break'> </span> baked a cake. That was <span class='line-break'> </span> our dinner. Vegetables <span class='line-break'> </span> has a bout dried up.<span class='line-break'> </span> John Ward had the team <span class='line-break'> </span> and went to Level Run<span class='line-break'> </span> to a big gathering of<span class='line-break'> </span> some sort.<span class='line-break'> </span> I gathered some berries.<span class='line-break'> </span> Intend making jellie<span class='line-break'> </span> tomorrow. The children <span class='line-break'> </span> are all in a glee<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight eating candy<span class='line-break'> </span> and blowing up their<span class='line-break'> </span> balloons. Good night. </p>

All of the men<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/283' title='plowing'>plowed</a> this morning. <span class='line-break'> </span> This evening <a href='../subjects/4' title='Benjamin Franklin Brumfield, Sr.'>Ben</a> and<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/9' title='Henry Anderson Brumfield'>Henry</a> went to <a href='../subjects/7208' title='Altavista, Virginia'>Altavista</a>.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben had his teeth worked <span class='line-break'> </span> on. Hope it may<span class='line-break'> </span> rain on all the places <span class='line-break'> </span> that need it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Ben helped Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> Farthing thresh wheat<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning and Bob Starkey<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. <div id="page-2461">
<h3><a name="page-2461">Monday, July  9, 1923</a></h3>

Then they eat dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Henry staid and<span class='line-break'> </span> played croqet. Jim come<span class='line-break'> </span> home. <div id="page-2462">

He<span class='line-break'> </span> got 25 pound of sugar. <span class='line-break'> </span> I made some jellie<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning. I picked<span class='line-break'> </span> a half gallon of berries<span class='line-break'> </span> and made a pie. I cooked<span class='line-break'> </span> cabbage and potatoes. <span class='line-break'> </span> This evening I picked<span class='line-break'> </span> a gallon of berries.<span class='line-break'> </span> I boiled them and put<span class='line-break'> </span> them to drain. The children<span class='line-break'> </span> wanted to go see <span class='line-break'> </span> Aunt Kate this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I did not feel like I<span class='line-break'> </span> could go and walk and<span class='line-break'> </span> there was no other <span class='line-break'> </span> way that I could go.<span class='line-break'> </span> I keep thinking that some<span class='line-break'> </span> one will come to see me.</p>

<div id="page-2463">
<h3><a name="page-2463">Wednesday, July 11, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day and very<span class='line-break'> </span> hot. The boys plowed<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco. Henry painted<span class='line-break'> </span> a little. The roof <span class='line-break'> </span> was so hot that he<span class='line-break'> </span> could not do much.<span class='line-break'> </span> My days work was a<span class='line-break'> </span> busy one. I washed<span class='line-break'> </span> dishes. Then got breakfast.<span class='line-break'> </span> Then milked the cows. I <span class='line-break'> </span> made some jellie. Parched<span class='line-break'> </span> coffee. Washed dished. Killed<span class='line-break'> </span> and dressed two chickens. <span class='line-break'> </span> Fried them for dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Baked bread and coffee. <span class='line-break'> </span> Then had dinner and <span class='line-break'> </span> washed dishes. Then<span class='line-break'> </span> rested a while. Then<span class='line-break'> </span> went and picked one<span class='line-break'> </span> gallon of berrie. Picked over<span class='line-break'> </span> and fixed them to make <span class='line-break'> </span> preserves. Fed the chickens. <span class='line-break'> </span> Then got supper and <span class='line-break'> </span> washed dishes. Now I am<span class='line-break'> </span> ready to go to bed.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2465">
<h3><a name="page-2465">Thursday, July 12, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good morning rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening the men<span class='line-break'> </span> plowed in their tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> Today Henry painted a<span class='line-break'> </span> little. Today I don't know<span class='line-break'> </span> much to write. No one has <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see us and we <span class='line-break'> </span> have not gone to see<span class='line-break'> </span> them. Would be glad<span class='line-break'> </span> to see all of my<span class='line-break'> </span> children and all of my<span class='line-break'> </span> neighbors. The weather is <span class='line-break'> </span> so hot that I can't <span class='line-break'> </span> do much of anything.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to Renan <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning for some<span class='line-break'> </span> bolts for the plows.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2464">
<h3><a name="page-2464">Friday, July 13, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A hot day. No rain yet.<span class='line-break'> </span> Today the men plowed<span class='line-break'> </span> in the crop. I don't know<span class='line-break'> </span> what. Ben went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Strait Stone for salt.<span class='line-break'> </span> I sent 7 doz eggs.<span class='line-break'> </span> All the children<span class='line-break'> </span> went with him. <span class='line-break'> </span> I done the same olde<span class='line-break'> </span> thing. Got dinner and<span class='line-break'> </span> churned. I cooked snaps.<span class='line-break'> </span> The last mess until<span class='line-break'> </span> some growes. Cooked potatoes<span class='line-break'> </span> and beets. Picked a half <span class='line-break'> </span> gallon of black berries.<span class='line-break'> </span> Had them with cream.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went and picked<span class='line-break'> </span> a gallon of berries and<span class='line-break'> </span> canned them. Berries<span class='line-break'> </span> are fine this time.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am so tired of<span class='line-break'> </span> staying here and so<span class='line-break'> </span> much expected of me.<span class='line-break'> </span> If I was young and<span class='line-break'> </span> strong it would be better.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2466">
<h3><a name="page-2466">Saturday, July 14, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>We had a hard cloud<span class='line-break'> </span> last night at midnight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lot of hard thunder and <span class='line-break'> </span> a hard rain and some wind.<span class='line-break'> </span> The land is washed level <span class='line-break'> </span> in some places. Ben and<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Mr. Booker went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Mr. Eleck Hutchersons<span class='line-break'> </span> and prised up some <span class='line-break'> </span> rock for cap rock on<span class='line-break'> </span> flues in the barn. They<span class='line-break'> </span> were hot and tierd when<span class='line-break'> </span> they got home. Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> and Hugh Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> and Mr. Mayhew and some<span class='line-break'> </span> of his boys went seign.<span class='line-break'> </span> They did not catch<span class='line-break'> </span> much. The creek was so<span class='line-break'> </span> mudy and high.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna and Franklin and Mabel<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Mr. Mayhews<span class='line-break'> </span> a little while. They had<span class='line-break'> </span> a nice time. They come <span class='line-break'> </span> home and brought water <span class='line-break'> </span> and wood. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2467">
<h3><a name="page-2467">Sunday, July 15, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Jim staid<span class='line-break'> </span> at home all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and the children went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Strait Stone to Sunday<span class='line-break'> </span> School and preaching. The<span class='line-break'> </span> Emerson children come<span class='line-break'> </span> home with them. I left<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner that they made <span class='line-break'> </span> some sort of a dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to George Blairs.<span class='line-break'> </span> There was no one at<span class='line-break'> </span> home. I set down in<span class='line-break'> </span> their porch and had<span class='line-break'> </span> not bin there long<span class='line-break'> </span> when Foy Pickerel and<span class='line-break'> </span> Ernest and Irvin Craddock<span class='line-break'> </span> come after me. Sister<span class='line-break'> </span> Mary[?] and Foy Pickerel and<span class='line-break'> </span> family and Irvin Craddock<span class='line-break'> </span> and family was there.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was very glad to see <span class='line-break'> </span> them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Henry went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Cedar Forest to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> The Billie Sunday club will<span class='line-break'> </span> be there.<span class='line-break'> </span>  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2468">
<h3><a name="page-2468">Monday, July 16, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy morning, rain <span class='line-break'> </span> at twelve oclock. Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> got up some rock. Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went to the mill. He got<span class='line-break'> </span> wet coming home. Had <span class='line-break'> </span> to change clothes. He eat<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner and him and Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Mr. Mayhews and play<span class='line-break'> </span> croquet. The Mayhews<span class='line-break'> </span> had supper be fore Ben and<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry come home. Said they<span class='line-break'> </span> had fresh fish. Mayhew<span class='line-break'> </span> went seining this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> and caught several fish.<span class='line-break'> </span> John Hutcherson run a<span class='line-break'> </span> gainst Clack Hubbards<span class='line-break'> </span> horse and brok his leg<span class='line-break'> </span> and then they killed<span class='line-break'> </span> the horse. I am sorry<span class='line-break'> </span> that it happened.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children and I caught<span class='line-break'> </span> a [?enty] young chickens<span class='line-break'> </span> and put them up. <span class='line-break'> </span> Will sell them soon <span class='line-break'> </span> I guess.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2469">
<h3><a name="page-2469">Tuesday, July 17, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. The men<span class='line-break'> </span> worked on their tobacco<span class='line-break'> </span> until dinner. Then Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> and Ben and Mr. Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Mr. Elleck <span class='line-break'> </span> Hutchensons to get up<span class='line-break'> </span> rock for their flues.<span class='line-break'> </span> They went on Mr. Booker's<span class='line-break'> </span> car. Kate Harvey and <span class='line-break'> </span> Virginia Thomson was<span class='line-break'> </span> here this evening. Irvin<span class='line-break'> </span> brought them and come<span class='line-break'> </span> for them. The children<span class='line-break'> </span> and I was fixing to go to<span class='line-break'> </span> see Kate and Virginia.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad that<span class='line-break'> </span> they come. We would of<span class='line-break'> </span> had to walk.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Henry and Edna has<span class='line-break'> </span> gone to Cedar Forest <span class='line-break'> </span> to night. I wish I <span class='line-break'> </span> could get to go some<span class='line-break'> </span> where and time to <span class='line-break'> </span> enjoy going. Work work <span class='line-break'> </span> work work <span class='line-break'> </span> and stay at home.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2471">
<h3><a name="page-2471">Wednesday, July 18, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Jim and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> worked on the barn flues<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning. This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> they plowed in the tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> I gathered some black<span class='line-break'> </span> berries for dinner. I <span class='line-break'> </span> had butter beans today<span class='line-break'> </span> for the first season<span class='line-break'> </span> I wanted to go fishing<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening but did <span class='line-break'> </span> not get to go.<span class='line-break'> </span> We had eat supper <span class='line-break'> </span> and I was about<span class='line-break'> </span> washing dishes when<span class='line-break'> </span> Gorden and Frances and Lizzie<span class='line-break'> </span> and Alma all Bennetts<span class='line-break'> </span> come come [sic]. I was <span class='line-break'> </span> glad to see them. <span class='line-break'> </span> They had bin to <span class='line-break'> </span> supper be fore they<span class='line-break'> </span> left home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alma is going to<span class='line-break'> </span> stay a while. She <span class='line-break'> </span> brought me a dress.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2470">
<h3><a name="page-2470">Thursday, July 19, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Ben and<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim plowed in the <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all the morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Ben and I and <span class='line-break'> </span> Franklin and Mabel <span class='line-break'> </span> went to White Falls. <span class='line-break'> </span> I fished some. Dr. Owen <span class='line-break'> </span> and family Doris and Janie<span class='line-break'> </span> Brumfield and Floid <span class='line-break'> </span> Reynols came to White<span class='line-break'> </span> Falls to bathe. Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> went with Mr. Mayhew<span class='line-break'> </span> seining. They caught a <span class='line-break'> </span> few nice fish. Alma<span class='line-break'> </span> Bennett dressed them <span class='line-break'> </span> for Henry. Edna got a <span class='line-break'> </span> letter from Mrs. Car <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. Alma made<span class='line-break'> </span> a dress for me today.<span class='line-break'> </span> They are playing the <span class='line-break'> </span> [phonegraph?]. I think it<span class='line-break'> </span> is time they went in <span class='line-break'> </span> bed.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2472">
<h3><a name="page-2472">Friday, July 20, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. The men<span class='line-break'> </span> hauled some flue wood <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning. This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry and John Ward went<span class='line-break'> </span> to the mill. They got their<span class='line-break'> </span> grinding. Jim and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> and I went to Gretna<span class='line-break'> </span> and to see Marvin<span class='line-break'> </span> and Carrie. We had a rough<span class='line-break'> </span> trip but I was glad<span class='line-break'> </span> to go. Alma Bennett<span class='line-break'> </span> is here. She has made<span class='line-break'> </span> the most of three<span class='line-break'> </span> dresses since yesterday. <span class='line-break'> </span> She got supper for me<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight. She is one handy<span class='line-break'> </span> girl. Oh how I wish <span class='line-break'> </span> I could see all of <span class='line-break'> </span> the children. Some of<span class='line-break'> </span> them that could come<span class='line-break'> </span> to see me won't<span class='line-break'> </span> come. Alma wants<span class='line-break'> </span> me to try on my <span class='line-break'> </span> new dresses.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2473">
<h3><a name="page-2473">Saturday, July 21, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. The boys<span class='line-break'> </span> went after rock this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning. This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Henry went with<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr. Mayhew seining.<span class='line-break'> </span> They caught several <span class='line-break'> </span> fish. Jim staid at home. <span class='line-break'> </span> Alma made another<span class='line-break'> </span> dress today. Jim found<span class='line-break'> </span> the first ripe tomato<span class='line-break'> </span> today. He gave it to<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel. <span class='line-break'> </span> I don't know any<span class='line-break'> </span> thing to write.<span class='line-break'> </span> We had snaps for <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner and some<span class='line-break'> </span> berries. The last for this<span class='line-break'> </span> season I guess.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2475">
<h3><a name="page-2475">Sunday, July 22, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Jim staid<span class='line-break'> </span> at home all day. Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Green Pond<span class='line-break'> </span> to a meeting. Irvin Harvy<span class='line-break'> </span> carried him. Alma<span class='line-break'> </span> and I and all the children<span class='line-break'> </span> s[t]aid here all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Dews Lanier and his wife<span class='line-break'> </span> and baby come to see us<span class='line-break'> </span> today. His wife was Fanny<span class='line-break'> </span> Emmerson. Lee and Grace <span class='line-break'> </span> and Hilder Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> come this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad to see them.<span class='line-break'> </span> I put on one of my<span class='line-break'> </span> new dresses this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Julia Fergerson was<span class='line-break'> </span> at home to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> She was going to<span class='line-break'> </span> Danvill today. I wish<span class='line-break'> </span> I could of seen Julia<span class='line-break'> </span> before she went. I hope<span class='line-break'> </span> she may be satisfied<span class='line-break'> </span> with her home. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2474">
<h3><a name="page-2474">Monday, July 23, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. I got breakfast<span class='line-break'> </span> and milked at home. Alma<span class='line-break'> </span> washed dishes. Then we <span class='line-break'> </span> caught 32 chickens and <span class='line-break'> </span> put them in a crate. Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> helped us. Then he brought<span class='line-break'> </span> the children and I to <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna and to Marvins.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went home. I am at<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins now. Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> washed this morning. <span class='line-break'> </span> I have set a round<span class='line-break'> </span> most of the day. Lee<span class='line-break'> </span> come by here. He did <span class='line-break'> </span> not stay long. <span class='line-break'> </span> I would like so much<span class='line-break'> </span> to know how they<span class='line-break'> </span> made out with the <span class='line-break'> </span> cow. I do hope they<span class='line-break'> </span> will make out well.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am feeling very well<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight. Hope all are<span class='line-break'> </span> well at home. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2477">
<h3><a name="page-2477">Tuesday, July 24, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Some rain today. We <span class='line-break'> </span> need it and more yet <span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie packed a nice <span class='line-break'> </span> lunch and Carrie and <span class='line-break'> </span> all the children and I<span class='line-break'> </span> started to go to Taylors <span class='line-break'> </span> Mill. It commenced to <span class='line-break'> </span> rain while we were at <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna. We went on<span class='line-break'> </span> until we near the<span class='line-break'> </span> mill and it rained <span class='line-break'> </span> so hard that we come <span class='line-break'> </span> home. We eat dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> at home and spent the<span class='line-break'> </span> evening mending the<span class='line-break'> </span> childrens clothes<span class='line-break'> </span> and going to the snap<span class='line-break'> </span> patch. Carrie had <span class='line-break'> </span> to take little Julia.<span class='line-break'> </span> That was a job on<span class='line-break'> </span> her. I have wrote a note <span class='line-break'> </span> home to night<span class='line-break'> </span> and so much hope that <span class='line-break'> </span> they are well at home.  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2476">
<h3><a name="page-2476">Wednesday, July 25, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> and the children<span class='line-break'> </span> and I went to Taylors<span class='line-break'> </span> Mill this morning. We<span class='line-break'> </span> fished a while and <span class='line-break'> </span> caught a few fish.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went<span class='line-break'> </span> in bathing and had <span class='line-break'> </span> a good time. <span class='line-break'> </span> We went home and<span class='line-break'> </span> then come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie. Carrie and all<span class='line-break'> </span> the children come<span class='line-break'> </span> with me. Found <span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie well and by <span class='line-break'> </span> her self. Gordon <span class='line-break'> </span> is staying at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> This week Frances<span class='line-break'> </span> is visiting her<span class='line-break'> </span> folks. I hope so<span class='line-break'> </span> much that all is<span class='line-break'> </span> well at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin's cow is <span class='line-break'> </span> sick. I hope she may<span class='line-break'> </span> get well. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2479">
<h3><a name="page-2479">Thursday, July 26, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. I am at<span class='line-break'> </span> Tim Bennetts. Eat breakfast<span class='line-break'> </span> and dinner here. Then <span class='line-break'> </span> Gorden carried Lizzie and<span class='line-break'> </span> I to Jo Towlers. Found <span class='line-break'> </span> them well and seemed <span class='line-break'> </span> to be doing well. Then<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Billie Bennetts.<span class='line-break'> </span> They were all well but <span class='line-break'> </span> Sister Nan[n]ie. She looks<span class='line-break'> </span> feeble. Jimmie and Bessie<span class='line-break'> </span> was there and Ella and <span class='line-break'> </span> Elender and Lizzie Bennett<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see us. I was <span class='line-break'> </span> glad that I met with <span class='line-break'> </span> them once more.<span class='line-break'> </span> Gordon come for us<span class='line-break'> </span> about sundown. <span class='line-break'> </span> We had a pleasant<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie got supper <span class='line-break'> </span> and milked. Gordon milked<span class='line-break'> </span> as she was late.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2478">
<h3><a name="page-2478">Friday, July 27, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. I was at Tim<span class='line-break'> </span> Bennetts this morning. Tim<span class='line-break'> </span> and four Negro men went to<span class='line-break'> </span> The Red House to day. Gordon<span class='line-break'> </span> Bennett brought me to Marvins.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie come with me. She<span class='line-break'> </span> went home on the train. <span class='line-break'> </span> I have had a good time<span class='line-break'> </span> with them. Lizzie and Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> think they have a hard time<span class='line-break'> </span> and they do but it might<span class='line-break'> </span> be worse. They have enough<span class='line-break'> </span> to eat and to wear. I <span class='line-break'> </span> wish they did not have to <span class='line-break'> </span> work so hard and they<span class='line-break'> </span> were more content<span class='line-break'> </span> with their lot. I would<span class='line-break'> </span> give them enough to do<span class='line-break'> </span> some good but I can't<span class='line-break'> </span> help mself or them <span class='line-break'> </span> either. I want to be<span class='line-break'> </span> thankful that I am able<span class='line-break'> </span> to do what I can.<span class='line-break'> </span> Oh Lord remember us all <span class='line-break'> </span> for Christ sake. Amen.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2480">
<h3><a name="page-2480">Saturday, July 28, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy morning. Rain<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening and tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> I come home this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and Carrie and four<span class='line-break'> </span> of the children come<span class='line-break'> </span> with me. I am thankful<span class='line-break'> </span> that he brought me.<span class='line-break'> </span> I found all at home<span class='line-break'> </span> getting on alright.<span class='line-break'> </span> I know that Alma<span class='line-break'> </span> done a lot of work.<span class='line-break'> </span> I had a good trip.<span class='line-break'> </span> Every one was kind <span class='line-break'> </span> to me. I went some<span class='line-break'> </span> where every day<span class='line-break'> </span> on their car.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie sent and<span class='line-break'> </span> got ice and made<span class='line-break'> </span> cream. We did enjoy<span class='line-break'> </span> it. I am glad that<span class='line-break'> </span> I am at home. The <span class='line-break'> </span> children was glad <span class='line-break'> </span> to see me.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2481">
<h3><a name="page-2481">Sunday, July 29, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. We all staid<span class='line-break'> </span> at home for dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alma got the dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> She is a wonder. I think<span class='line-break'> </span> she has kept house for <span class='line-break'> </span> me a week and all of <span class='line-break'> </span> the children like her.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and the children<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Jim Powers.<span class='line-break'> </span> Found them well.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Car was at<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr. Powers. No one<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see us today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alma spent the <span class='line-break'> </span> evening reading.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am a fraid that<span class='line-break'> </span> Franklin is not well.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry has gone to <span class='line-break'> </span> George Emersons tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Heard today that<span class='line-break'> </span> there was a good <span class='line-break'> </span> rain.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2483">
<h3><a name="page-2483">Monday, July 30, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good morning. Rain <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. Ben worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on the truck most of the<span class='line-break'> </span> day. He went to Srait<span class='line-break'> </span> Stone for some bolts. He<span class='line-break'> </span> let all of the children<span class='line-break'> </span> go. Jim sowed some<span class='line-break'> </span> turnip seed and got up<span class='line-break'> </span> some potatoes. <span class='line-break'> </span> Alma got most of the<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. We had snaps<span class='line-break'> </span> and butter beans and corn.<span class='line-break'> </span> The first that we have <span class='line-break'> </span> had this season. Alma<span class='line-break'> </span> made me two aprons<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening and changed<span class='line-break'> </span> Ednas dress. <span class='line-break'> </span> Alma went to Blains<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening to spend<span class='line-break'> </span> the night. I will miss<span class='line-break'> </span> her so much when she<span class='line-break'> </span> goes home and she intends <span class='line-break'> </span> going soon. Franklin <span class='line-break'> </span> has bin complaining all <span class='line-break'> </span> the evening.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2482">
<h3><a name="page-2482">Tuesday, July 31, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A heavy rain last night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Cloudy all day. Rain again<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight. We want it to<span class='line-break'> </span> quit raining now as bad<span class='line-break'> </span> as we wanted it to<span class='line-break'> </span> rain. Jim and Ben and John<span class='line-break'> </span> Ward and Henry worked on<span class='line-break'> </span> the bridge over the branch<span class='line-break'> </span> most of the day. Jim and Henry <span class='line-break'> </span> went to Mount Airy for <span class='line-break'> </span> lumber to make the <span class='line-break'> </span> bridge. They carried a <span class='line-break'> </span> log to Starkeys mill.<span class='line-break'> </span> They got wet before<span class='line-break'> </span> they got home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alma come from<span class='line-break'> </span> George Blains today.<span class='line-break'> </span> She said that they<span class='line-break'> </span> had commenced on <span class='line-break'> </span> the new school<span class='line-break'> </span> house. Henry tried to<span class='line-break'> </span> milk tonight. I hope he<span class='line-break'> </span> may learn. Edna can<span class='line-break'> </span> milk ok.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2485">
<h3><a name="page-2485">Wednesday, August  1, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy morning. Clear<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. The men suckered<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco today. Alma wanted<span class='line-break'> </span> to go home. Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> her home. He let me and <span class='line-break'> </span> three children went<span class='line-break'> </span> with him. We found<span class='line-break'> </span> them well at Jims. We<span class='line-break'> </span> stopped at Gretna and <span class='line-break'> </span> bought a few things.<span class='line-break'> </span> We got home in good<span class='line-break'> </span> time. Johnson stopped <span class='line-break'> </span> and looked at the phone. <span class='line-break'> </span> Said he would come<span class='line-break'> </span> in the morning and fix<span class='line-break'> </span> it up. I will miss<span class='line-break'> </span> Alma. She cooked and<span class='line-break'> </span> helped me so good. <span class='line-break'> </span> The children all<span class='line-break'> </span> like Alma. She was<span class='line-break'> </span> so good to them<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben said she fed<span class='line-break'> </span> them good while I <span class='line-break'> </span> was a way. Ben and Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> milked this morning.</p>

<div id="page-2484">
<h3><a name="page-2484">Thursday, August  2, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Very warm.<span class='line-break'> </span> The men hauled logs<span class='line-break'> </span> to the saw mill all <span class='line-break'> </span> day. I staid at home<span class='line-break'> </span> today and done the work. <span class='line-break'> </span> I cooked snaps and corn<span class='line-break'> </span> and potatoes. Went to the <span class='line-break'> </span> corn field for snaps. Could<span class='line-break'> </span> not get them. Johnson<span class='line-break'> </span> Reynolds come this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning and fixed the <span class='line-break'> </span> pohn. Mollie come<span class='line-break'> </span> with him. I was glad<span class='line-break'> </span> that she come. It had<span class='line-break'> </span> been so long since<span class='line-break'> </span> she was here.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim pulled a water<span class='line-break'> </span> mellon this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> It was not ripe good. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben gave the <span class='line-break'> </span> children some <span class='line-break'> </span> medicine tonight. <span class='line-break'> </span> I wrote two letters<span class='line-break'> </span> today. One to John. One to Carrie.</p>

<div id="page-2487">
<h3><a name="page-2487">Friday, August  3, 1923</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day most of the<span class='line-break'> </span> day. Had a shower just at<span class='line-break'> </span> night. Ben hauled some<span class='line-break'> </span> logs for him self this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning and helped Norman<span class='line-break'> </span> Booker this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim spent the day a<span class='line-break'> </span> way from home today<span class='line-break'> </span> for the first time in a <span class='line-break'> </span> long time. The <span class='line-break'> </span> paper tolde of the <span class='line-break'> </span> P[?]sadens death. That is <span class='line-break'> </span> a sad ending to his<span class='line-break'> </span> trip.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

I was glad<span class='line-break'> </span> to get home so easy<span class='line-break'> </span> but if I could help<span class='line-break'> </span> my self I would not<span class='line-break'> </span> be any trouble or<span class='line-break'> </span> expence to any one.</p>
